# Platform Build Log

Append-only log of work sessions. Each session adds exactly one row, in two edits:

1. **At session start** (before any real work): append a row with status `⏳ IN FLIGHT — {step name}`, commit it immediately as its own standalone commit.
2. **At session end** (after the real work is done, tested, and typechecked): update that same row to `✅ DONE — {step name}`, filling in the real commit hash of the work, then commit the update (either folded into the final commit or immediately after it).

If a session dies, crashes, or is abandoned mid-way, its row stays `⏳ IN FLIGHT`, which is itself the record that an attempt was made and didn't finish.

See [CLAUDE.md](CLAUDE.md) for the exact instructions.

| Date | Status | Step | Commit |
|------|--------|------|--------|
| 2026-07-23 | ✅ DONE | URGENT — Tenant-Signals Import Never Persists to Database. Traced the real import path end to end: `/admin-panel/delivery/tenant-signals`'s Import modal (`TenantSignals.tsx` `handleImport`) posts to `POST /api/admin/signal-rules/import` (admin-signal-rules.ts), which deletes all platform-owned (`msp_id IS NULL`) rows and re-inserts every rule/group from the pasted JSON inside one `db.transaction`. `signal_key`, `rule_type`, and `source_key` are `NOT NULL` columns on `signal_derivation_rules` (lib/db schema) — but the endpoint inserted `r.signalKey ?? r.signal_key` etc. straight into the `INSERT` with no validation. A single row in a 36-rule payload missing or misnaming one of those fields throws a Postgres NOT NULL violation mid-transaction, rolling back the *entire* import to zero rows written, caught by a blanket `catch` that returned a generic `500 "Import failed"` — genuinely indistinguishable from silent no-op, matching exactly what was observed (`id BETWEEN 1001 AND 1037` → 0 rows). Also independently confirmed the endpoint never honored incoming `id` values in the payload anyway (rows are always assigned fresh serial IDs on insert), so "ids 1001-1037" could never have landed as literal IDs even on a successful import — not the failure itself, but worth knowing. FIX: added pre-transaction validation that checks every rule has `signalKey`/`ruleType`/`sourceKey` (and every group has `signalKey`) *before* the destructive DELETE+INSERT runs, returning a `400` that lists every failing row index and field by name instead of a blind rollback; also changed the catch handler to surface the real DB error message instead of the generic string, for any failure mode validation doesn't catch. New `admin-signal-rules-import.test.ts` (registered in `vitest.config.ts`'s hardcoded include list) verifies: a payload missing `sourceKey` is rejected with a 400 naming the row *and the transaction is never entered* (zero DB writes attempted); same for missing `signalKey`; a well-formed payload reaches the transaction and reports the correct imported count. `npx tsc --noEmit` in `artifacts/api-server` clean; new test file 3/3 passing in isolation; full suite run shows 198 pre-existing failures across 33 unrelated files (`logger.child is not a function` in msp-portal/captcha, a pre-existing mission-control severity mismatch) — confirmed pre-existing and unrelated via `git status` showing only this task's 3 files touched. **Real, separate follow-up for Shane, NOT fixed here**: every one of the 36 rules in the payload that triggered this investigation has `weight: 0` and `pricingImpact: 0` — once persistence is fixed, these rules still produce zero pillar/pricing impact at weight 0 and need real, non-zero values from Shane to have any actual effect on signal-derived pricing or pillar coverage; no values were fabricated or defaulted here. No live DB access in this environment (per repo rule) — a real test import actually landing rows in `signal_derivation_rules` is confirmed only at the mocked-transaction level; Shane should re-attempt the real 36-rule import and confirm live. — commit `92abe6ed` |

| 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | License-Gap Classification — Unblock Docs, Honest Copy, Real Upsell — a real cross-cutting fix for tenants missing M365 add-ons (no Entra ID Premium / Defender for Office 365), a common real-customer situation. ROOT CAUSE (traced, not assumed): Graph checks that fail because the tenant lacks a SKU were conflated with two unrelated states. Either way `pkgResult.runStatus` became `consent_revoked`/`partial_failure`, so `diagnostics-runner`'s `finalStatus` never reached `"completed"` — and the seeded Assessment Document Generation workflow's `assessment_doc_gate` requires `msp_diagnostic_runs.status = 'completed'`, so a license-gapped tenant could NEVER get documents generated. (D3) `portal-assessment.ts` exposes `checksLicenseGap` + `licenseGapFeatures` from the run/summary; `AssessmentWizard.tsx` scan-complete copy now reads e.g. "9 checks passed. | 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | Fix Typewriter Headline Randomization + Repeat Bug — confirmed root cause of both bugs by tracing `useHeroHeadlines.ts` + the seed SQL: `FALLBACK_HEADLINE`'s text is byte-identical to the DB's `sort_order = 0` row (`2026-07-19-hero-headlines.sql`), and the hook seeded `headlines` state to `[FALLBACK_HEADLINE]` (array length 1) before the `/api/public/hero-headlines` fetch resolved. Since `headlineIndex % headlines.length` is always `0 % 1 = 0`, the rotation was trapped on that single entry — typing, pausing, and deleting it in a full loop, potentially more than once — for however long the fetch took; because that entry's text is identical to the real first headline, this was visually indistinguishable from "the first headline plays twice" before the real rotation ever started. Separately, `public-hero.ts` always returned rows `orderBy(asc(sortOrder))` and nothing on the client ever reordered them, so rotation order was always fixed DB order. FIX: added a `loaded` flag set once the fetch settles (success, empty, or failure); while unloaded and still on the 1-element fallback array, the typing effect now holds at the fully-typed fallback instead of deleting/retyping it in a loop. On successful fetch, the headline set is now shuffled once (Fisher-Yates) before being stored, and `headlineIndex`/`charCount`/`phase` are reset so the real rotation starts clean at a random order — not re-shuffled on every cycle, only once per page load. Only `useHeroHeadlines.ts` touched — `Home.tsx`, the admin Hero Headlines management screen, and headline content untouched, per task scope. `shane-mccaw-consulting` typechecks clean (`npx tsc -p tsconfig.json --noEmit`, exit 0). Not clicked through in a live browser in this environment (no dev server running this session) — verified by full code trace of the fetch → state → effect chain plus the confirmed seed-data match, and clean typecheck. | 2621845e |

OPPORTUNITY ranking reuses the real Sales Offer Engine output (no new scoring invented): open (draft/sent) sales_offers summed by adjusted (customer-facing) price with base-price fallback — sales_offers.customerId is a users.id, bridged back to msp_customers.id via msp_users (the same billing-attribution bridge omg-card-extractor uses). Staff tenant-access scoping folded into every query at the DB level exactly like msp-alerts.ts (resolveMspIdStrict + resolveStaffScopedCustomerIds; scopedIds===null = unrestricted). QBR DESIGN DECISION (per task): built a SINGLE cross-customer whole-book document per (mspId, quarter), NOT a per-customer bundle — the per-customer client-facing formal doc already exists (consolidated SOW → insights_generated_documents, customerId-scoped); the leadership view's job is the cross-book roll-up the SOW deliberately isn't. QBR GENERATION-CONVENTION DECISION (per task): chose the consolidated-sow-generator convention (shared anthropic client STREAMING with claude-opus-4-8, DB-editable getPrompt() with hard-coded fallback, HTML output via extractAiHtml, generating→ready/failed status lifecycle) over the light OMG-card/dashboard-executive-summary one, BECAUSE a QBR is a long formal client-ready document and the Haiku summarizers cap at 800 tokens of JSON — far too small; BUT layered in the two disciplines the SOW generator omits, borrowed from dashboard-executive-summary.ts: recordAiUsage() cost telemetry (nodeType partner_qbr, costOwner msp) and a HARD cache so an expensive Opus generation is never run speculatively (one QBR per quarter; a view returns the cached row, force overwrites in place). insights_generated_documents can't hold an MSP-level doc (its customerId FK is a single users.id, no mspId), so NEW MSP-scoped msp_partner_qbrs table (unique on mspId+quarterKey = the cache/upsert key). Routes: GET /api/msp/executive (MSPOperator+, scoped lists), GET+POST /api/msp/executive/qbr (MSPAdmin+ — whole-book leadership artifact, intentionally not staff-scoped). | 2026-07-20 | ✅ DONE | Per-Statement SQL Results — the simulator SQL console + manual-migration runner now report each statement in a multi-statement script separately (SSMS-style) instead of only the last statement's result surfacing (Postgres runs the whole batch but node-pg returns only the final result). New `sql-statement-splitter.ts` — a real SQL-aware splitter on top-level semicolons that skips semicolons inside single-quoted literals (`''` escape), double-quoted identifiers (`""` escape), dollar-quoted blocks (`$$`/`$tag$`, with `$1` params correctly NOT treated as dollar quotes), `--` line comments, and nestable `/* */` block comments; keeps a trailing unterminated statement; drops whitespace/comment-only segments; leaves BEGIN/COMMIT as their own statements so wrapped scripts replay correctly. 16 unit tests (added to the hardcoded vitest include list) cover every case, all green. `executeRawSql()` rewritten: splits the script, runs each statement in its own `client.query()` round-trip on a SINGLE `pool.connect()` connection (so a `BEGIN;…;COMMIT;` script genuinely shares one transaction), catches errors per-statement so statement N failing doesn't stop N+1, and returns `{ statements: [{ statementIndex, statementText (≤500-char preview), success, rows, rowCount, fields, executionMs, error? }] }`; a best-effort `ROLLBACK` in `finally` guarantees a half-open/aborted transaction is never handed back to the pool (no-op warning otherwise). | 2026-07-19 | ✅ DONE | Real Account Lockout — customer-team.tsx's isLockedOut/handleUnlock was pure client-side state with zero backend and no schema concept of lockout at all. Added real failed-login tracking on msp_users (failedLoginAttempts, lastFailedLoginAt, lockedUntil — manual SQL, not yet applied) since usersTable has no per-tenant team concept and legacy platform-admin users (no msp_users row) intentionally stay lockout-exempt, matching the existing mfaEnforced precedent. Threshold: 5 failed passwords within a 15-minute window locks the account for 15 minutes (ACCOUNT_LOCKOUT_THRESHOLD/_WINDOW_MINUTES/_DURATION_MINUTES env-overridable, hardcoded defaults otherwise) — chosen as a standard, conservative anti-brute-force default; deliberately looser than the existing per-IP loginLimiter (10/15min) since this is a second, per-account layer, not a replacement. /auth/login now checks lockedUntil before the bcrypt compare (blocks with 423 + accountLocked:true, no password-validity signal leaked) and increments/locks on each bad password (423 the moment the threshold is crossed) — mirrors the mfaEnforced pattern of returning before token issuance, both now sharing one consolidated mspUsersTable lookup instead of two. A correct password always resets the counter/lock, so 1-2 mistyped attempts followed by success never trips lockout. Real unlock: POST /portal/team/:userId/unlock (portal.ts), ownership-scoped via assertCustomerAccess against the target's own customerId exactly like the sibling status/mfa-enforcement/reset-mfa handlers, resets failedLoginAttempts/lastFailedLoginAt/lockedUntil and audit-logs team_member_unlocked. New `lib/defender-endpoint.ts` is a THIRD Microsoft resource audience layered on the SAME multi-tenant App Registration graph.ts already drives — NOT Microsoft Graph. Read graph.ts in full first and replicated its patterns exactly rather than inventing a parallel mechanism: token acquisition modeled on `getAccessTokenForTenant`/`getActivityApiToken` (v2.0 `client_credentials` `.default` flow reusing the SAME `MT_APP_CLIENT_ID`/`MT_APP_CLIENT_SECRET` env credentials — confirmed via code read those are the shared client-secret creds, no certificate and no duplicate secret storage), a per-tenant `Map<string,TokenCache>` identical in shape to graph.ts's `tenantTokenCache`/`activityTokenCache`, and the `graphWriteForTenant` typed-result convention. AUDIT-FIRST findings, all verified directly against current Microsoft Learn API reference (2025-11/2026-02 revisions), not guessed: (1) isolate = `POST https://api.security.microsoft.com/api/machines/{id}/isolate`, body `{ Comment (required), IsolationType: "Full"|"Selective"|"UnManagedDevice" }`, Application permission `Machine.Isolate`; (2) release-from-isolation = `POST .../unisolate`, body `{ Comment }`, same `Machine.Isolate` permission; (3) run-AV-scan = `POST .../runAntiVirusScan`, body `{ Comment (required), ScanType: "Quick"|"Full" }`, Application permission `Machine.Scan` (confirmed the real permission name — NOT a guessed "Machine.RunAntivirus"). All three return 201 Created + a MachineAction resource (typed). These permissions are granted under the **WindowsDefenderATP** API surface in the app registration, SEPARATE from Microsoft Graph — so documented them in a new exported `REQUIRED_DEFENDER_APP_PERMISSIONS` const in this file, deliberately NOT added to graph.ts's `REQUIRED_MT_SCOPES` (that is the Graph `.default` consent set; mixing a non-Graph scope in would break Graph token acquisition), with a comment that adding them forces fresh admin re-consent on every tenant. CRITICAL TOKEN-AUDIENCE GOTCHA baked in with a citing comment (Microsoft's own docs): the token scope is the LEGACY resource `https://api.securitycenter.microsoft.com/.default` even though the request host is `api.security.microsoft.com` — a mismatched audience returns 403 even against the right endpoint; do not "fix" the mismatch. Regional host variants (`us.`/`eu.`) overridable via `DEFENDER_ENDPOINT_API_BASE` env without a code change. DELIBERATE DESIGN DECISION (operational-risk-driven): Defender consent errors throw a dedicated `DefenderConsentError` and do NOT call graph.ts's `markTenantConsentRevoked` — Defender permission consent is a SEPARATE consent surface from the shared Graph `tenant_consent` row, and a tenant with valid Graph consent but no Defender re-consent returns AADSTS65001; flipping the Graph consent row there would wrongly disable working Graph monitoring (the exact collateral damage this integration must avoid). This layer evicts only its own token cache. All three write functions require a non-empty operator `Comment` (Microsoft requires it + it is Defender's audit trail); 403-insufficient-privilege / 409-conflict / "already in progress" / 404 surfaced as typed non-throwing results, only re-consent and network errors propagate. `integration.defender` added as a new leaf channel under the existing `integration.*` taxonomy (task-sanctioned). Documented 100 calls/min + 1,500/hr rate limits in a comment; no rate-limiting infra built (out of scope) — just a "don't call in a tight loop" note. api-server typechecks clean (only the pre-existing `health-engine.test.ts` TS2698 debt remains, consistent with prior sessions; zero Defender-related errors). | 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | Investigate --text-secondary Token Contrast — real-device feedback (screenshot) showed text still reading too dark/low-contrast even where components correctly use `text-secondary` (confirmed via code read, e.g. `DeliverablesList.tsx`), despite the token passing WCAG AA on paper. Root cause: the token's own color value, not misapplied classes — prior audit already confirmed correct class usage everywhere. Calculated real contrast ratios (WCAG relative-luminance formula, Node) for `--rebuild-text-secondary` against both `--charcoal-0` (`#1A1A1C`) and `--charcoal-1` (`#232326`): old `#9A9AA3` = 6.23:1 / 5.62:1 (AA pass, AAA fail on charcoal-1). Tested a ladder of brighter candidates and picked `#B5B5BC` = 8.52:1 / 7.69:1 — clears AAA (7:1) on both backgrounds, keeps the same cool-neutral hue ratio (B-channel ~7-9 above R/G, matching the original's tint) so it reads as the same color family just brighter, and stays a clear step below `--text-primary` (`#F5F5F7`, ~14:1) so the secondary/primary hierarchy is preserved — not pure white. | 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE — Site-Wide Forced-Refresh Bug: Root Cause Investigation — root-caused via live Playwright (not a guess) and DISPROVED the shared/global-component hypothesis: there is NO browser-reload path anywhere in the app (exhaustive grep + full read of every Layout-mounted component — no `location.reload`, no `<meta http-equiv=refresh>`, no service worker, no chunk-error reload handler, no error boundary; the only scroll listeners are BackToTop setting a bool + the analytics tracker firing beacons; recharts, Governance's only lazy import, is pre-bundled at Vite's startup scan so scroll-to-chart never re-optimizes). CONFIRMED ROOT CAUSE: a **Vite dev-server HMR full-page reload**, issued whenever a CONCURRENT editor/session saves a source module in the root import chain (or one whose HMR update can't be accepted and propagates to the entry) — it reloads EVERY open tab at once, independent of page or scroll position. The scroll correlation is coincidental (Governance/Monitoring are long multi-second reads, so a background file-save lands mid-scroll). EVIDENCE (live Playwright, 3 full down+up scroll passes/page): production build (vite build+preview, no HMR) = 0 reloads on both pages fully rendered; isolated single dev server (own cold cacheDir, own port) = 0 reloads on both; shared 5-server dev env = reloads seen but uncorrelated with scroll, with a concurrent session's `[vite] hot updated: Monitoring.tsx`+`index.css` observed live mid-test. DEFINITIVE controlled experiment: two tabs held STILL mid-page, then saving `src/main.tsx` (entry) → FULL RELOAD on BOTH tabs (docLoads 1→2, `[vite] connecting…` reboot) with zero scrolling; saving `analytics.ts`/`button.tsx`/`utils.ts` → app-wide `[vite] invalidate … Could not Fast Refresh` on both idle tabs. Amplifiers (dev-experience only, not user-facing): 5 concurrent dev servers sharing one `node_modules/.vite` cache; Fast-Refresh-incompatible mixed exports in `usePersonalizationState.tsx` (global, consumed by Layout on every page), `button.tsx`/`badge.tsx`/`form.tsx`. NO app code changed — per the task's own "no speculative fix" guardrail and because the reproduced cause is a dev-environment artifact absent from production, there is nothing to fix in runtime code (a save to a genuine root module always full-reloads — correct Vite behavior). Full write-up + reproduction steps in `artifacts/shane-mccaw-consulting/FORCED_REFRESH_INVESTIGATION.md`. Did NOT touch concurrent sessions' dirty files (Home.tsx et al.) or their stray `__*.mjs`/`vite_*.log` probes. | 1bc94616 |

| 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | URGENT: Fix Checkout Bypassing Stripe for Paid Package — CONFIRMED ROOT CAUSE (code-traced end-to-end; no DB access in this env so the specific live row was not queried, but the fix is correct for EVERY price-field combination so it does not depend on that): the public checkout's entire free-vs-paid pipeline read ONLY the legacy decimal `services.price`/`base_price` columns and IGNORED the canonical `services.price_cents`. The modern admin "create service" endpoint (`admin-services.ts` POST) writes ONLY `price_cents` and leaves `price`/`base_price` NULL, so any paid service created that way has `price=NULL, base_price=NULL, price_cents=<real>`. For such a row surfaced as an assessment offer, `GET /api/catalog/assessments` computed `isFree = isFreeOffering || (price ?? basePrice) == null || … === 0` → NULL → **isFree=true**. Only `AssessmentOffer` carries `isFree` to the storefront (`MonitoringTier` has NO isFree field at all — proven in `useCatalog.ts`, so a true monitoring_tier can never free-route; Shane's "monitoring package" is catalog serviceType=`assessment`, the tenant-scan product), so `tierToService` set `service.isFree=true`, the checkout button routed to `handleFreeCheckout` → `POST /api/portal/checkout/free` (NO Stripe), and `provisionFreeOnboarding` provisioned the account + session + tenant scan + confirmation email for $0 — matching every observed symptom. The EXISTING server guard in `provisionFreeOnboarding` failed for the same reason: it summed `s.price ?? s.basePrice` (→ $0 for a price_cents-only row) so it did not reject. Confirmed the paid path had the identical gap in THREE more spots (create-session `missingPrices` + `rawPriceCents`, and the contract `computedFinalPrice` which only runs when `basePrice` is set). FIX (single root cause = legacy-only price reading; one commit `0f4c81ac`): (1) new `resolveServicePriceCents()` + `isServiceFree()` in `catalog-pricing.ts` as the single source of truth (price_cents first, then legacy price/base_price; free only when isFreeOffering OR zero across every field); (2) `/catalog/assessments` derives isFree via `isServiceFree` and surfaces the real retail price for display when legacy columns are null but price_cents is set (so a paid assessment shows "$250", not "$0"); (3) `provisionFreeOnboarding` (serves BOTH `/portal/checkout/free` and `/portal/onboarding/claim-free`) now rejects any service where `!isServiceFree(s)` with a warn log — the mandated hardened defensive guard, a second independent enforcement point behind the frontend routing that holds even if that routing is ever wrong again; (4) create-session `missingPrices` + `rawPriceCents` now honor `price_cents` as a fallback so the paid path charges the real amount instead of erroring "no price configured"/charging $0. Verified correct across all four data states (price_cents-only paid, legacy paid, genuinely free, isFreeOffering promo) — the free assessment funnel stays free, only genuinely-priced items flip to Stripe. VERIFIED: `tsc --noEmit` clean on both `api-server` and `shane-mccaw-consulting`; new `catalog-pricing.test.ts` regression suite 13/13 pass (added the file to the vitest hardcoded include list — it and the pre-existing catalog-pricing tests were never actually running in CI). now ALSO fed by `deriveMonitorFindings`: one string per check whose latest row genuinely evaluated (status "ok") AND matched a severity condition, formatted `"<checkKey>: <severity> severity condition matched on latest monitoring scan (N items)"` — checkKey carries the real keyword surface (sharepoint:anonymous-links → "SharePoint"); | 2026-07-22 | ✅ DONE | Add security to HEALTH_PILLARS — Currently Defined But Never Computed — STOPPED AT DELIVERABLE 1 PER THE TASK'S OWN INSTRUCTION: investigation found the exclusion is DELIBERATE and documented, and adding "security" to HEALTH_PILLARS would DOUBLE-COUNT security platform-wide. The health-engine.ts file header (lines 11–19) explicitly documents the architecture: security is scored by the standalone Security Engine (security-engine.ts, real and working — sums the same securityImpact field over fired signals), and `calculateArchitectureHealthScore` combines the two one level up: final score = healthResult.score + securityResult.score, final breakdown = healthResult's 6 entries + securityResult's appended security entry. So the combined 7-pillar breakdown ALREADY contains a real, computed security score. If "security" were added to HEALTH_PILLARS, computeHealthEngine would sum securityImpact into its own score, then calculateArchitectureHealthScore would add securityResult.score AGAIN → total double-counted, breakdown would carry TWO "security" entries (breaking every `.find(b => b.pillar === ...)` consumer), and the health engine would emit a securityHealthContribution workflow variable duplicating the security engine's output. Downstream consumers explicitly encode the 6+1 contract: portal-mission-control.ts ("6 HEALTH_PILLARS entries plus the security entry calculateArchitectureHealthScore appends"), usePersonalizationData.ts (marketing site — already receives the real 7-pillar breakdown incl. security via /portal/mission-control/engines), solutionsTopics.ts ("HEALTH_PILLARS + the Security Engine's security pillar"), dashboard-resolvers.ts (security is its own SNAPSHOT_ENGINE_KEYS row, deliberately excluded from its local health-breakdown pillar set), health-engine.test.ts (sum expectations exclude security). THE REAL cause of /assessment-test's permanent "Not covered by this scan" Security gauge is NOT the engine — it's the DISPLAY/COVERAGE layer: pillar-coverage.ts `getPillarCoverage` iterates HEALTH_PILLARS (6) and its PILLAR_LABELS map has no security key, and health-display.ts `computeDisplayHealth` also iterates HEALTH_PILLARS — so both drop the security entry that the combined breakdown already carries. | 2026-07-22 | ✅ DONE | URGENT — Fix Hard Build Failure From Missing generated/version.json — confirmed live cause first, exactly as reported: `app-shell.tsx` (and the equivalent static import in `StatusBar.tsx`/`Footer.tsx`/`version.ts`) does a top-level `import versionInfo from "@/generated/version.json"`, and `scripts/generate-version.mjs` writes that file via each app's `predev`/`prebuild` npm-lifecycle hooks — but the file is deliberately `.gitignore`d, so if that hook never runs, the import target genuinely doesn't exist on disk and Vite/esbuild hard-fail the whole build at import-analysis, not at runtime. D1 investigation: this repo's `.replit` `[[workflows.workflow]]` "Project" run-button config (the only committed environment-startup definition found) only runs `check-drift` and `typecheck` shell tasks — it never invokes `pnpm run dev`/`vite` for any of the four apps at all, so there is no committed mechanism here that would reliably trigger `predev` before a dev server starts. That is the concrete, confirmed mechanism by which the generated file can be (and was) absent even though the generator script itself is correct and unmodified. Root cause: monitoring tiers carry their ENTIRE price in `type_attributes` (`pricePerUserMonth` × max(seats, `seatCountFloor`) + optional `flatMonthlySurcharge`) — the admin monitoring-tier editor writes no flat price at all (`priceFixed: false`), so `price`/`basePrice`/`priceCents` are all NULL on a real monitoring_tier row — and BOTH free-vs-paid gates read only those flat columns: (1) msp-portal consent-success.tsx `serviceIsFree` — every direct purchase lands there post-consent (consent precedes payment in this funnel) — judged the paid tier free, rendered "Free — no payment required" and inline-finalized via `/portal/onboarding/contract` + `/portal/checkout/free`, never reaching the public checkout's Stripe step; (2) `provisionFreeOnboarding`'s `isServiceFree` server guard had the identical blind spot and passed it, provisioning account + $0 invoice + setup email (tenant scan already running from consent). The prior investigation's "MonitoringTier can never free-route" claim only examined Checkout.tsx's `tierToService` gate — consent-success is a second, independent free/paid router it never examined. create-session (the actual charge path) already computed `pricePerUserMonth × seats` correctly; the defect was purely in the free/paid decision, never the charge amount. Fix: new `resolveTypeAttributesMonthlyPriceCents` in catalog-pricing.ts; `isServiceFree` now requires zero across the flat columns AND the typeAttributes model (also covers recurring_addon `flatMonthlyPrice`), fixing the server guard with no call-site changes (full DB rows already carry typeAttributes); consent-success `serviceIsFree` mirrors it via the typeAttributes already returned by `/api/services`. Reproduced + verified via Playwright against the real consent-success page with the API route-mocked to the real row shape (priceCents/price/basePrice NULL, ppu 8.00, floor 5, 25 seats = $200/mo): pre-fix = FREE ROUTE, `/portal/checkout/free` fired (bug reproduced); post-fix = "Continue to checkout", free-checkout never fired. vitest 23/23 (13 new incl. the exact real row shape); api-server tsc clean; msp-portal tsc shows only the known pre-existing customer-dashboard.tsx:202 error. |
